## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration of an oscillator and depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t through forcing or parametric modulation. This matches standard second-order ODE oscillator models written as x' = v and v' = dv_dt = f(x,v,t), including nonlinear restoring forces and nonlinear damping.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (undriven) harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Pendulum equation (no small-angle approximation): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (angular oscillator with nonlinear restoring torque)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with periodic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (chaos/bi-stability regimes)
- Van der Pol oscillator (nonlinear damping / self-excitation): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (limit-cycle oscillator)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillations)
- Nonlinear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic drag / amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Nonlinear stiffness with quintic term: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear springs)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * x - c4 * v (time-varying stiffness, parametric resonance)
- Liénard form (general nonlinear oscillator template): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (broad class including Van der Pol-like dynamics)
- Conservative dynamics from a potential energy: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (no damping/forcing; acceleration is minus potential gradient)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no t), typically as an odd function of x for symmetric potentials (e.g., -x, -x - x^3).
- Linear viscous damping: a term proportional to -v yields exponential decay of energy in the small-amplitude regime; nonlinear damping often appears as -v*Abs(v) or -v^3.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: adding -x^3 with positive coefficient increases oscillation frequency with amplitude (hardening), while negative coefficient decreases it (softening).
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior: damping that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c - x^2)*v or (c - v^2)*v, injects energy at small amplitude and removes it at large amplitude.
- Periodic external forcing: additive terms like cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicate driven response, resonance peaks, and possible chaotic motion when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric excitation: time-periodic modulation multiplying x (or multiplying an x-dependent stiffness term) suggests Mathieu-type instability tongues and parametric resonance.
- Symmetry cue: if dv_dt(x,v,t) is odd in x and odd in v (with no constant offsets), dynamics are typically centered about x=0 with no static bias; constant or even-in-x terms imply equilibrium shifts.
- Velocity-only nonlinearities: dependence primarily on v (e.g., (c - v^2)*v) indicates damping/drag-dominated dynamics, often affecting waveform shape more than equilibrium location.
- Polynomial restoring-force hierarchy: dominance of x, then x^3, then x^5 terms often corresponds to weakly to strongly nonlinear regimes; the lowest-order nonlinearity usually controls amplitude-dependent frequency.
